<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="population-studies">POPULATION STUDIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#population-studies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Demography is scientific study of human population</p>
<p>It focuses on 3 phenomena:</p>
<p>i. Changes in population size
ii. Composition of population
iii. Population distribution in space</p>
<p>Important ‘demographic processes’ include: fertility, mortality, marriage, education &amp; social mobility</p>
<p>In a broader sense, additional characteristics such as ethnicity (race, mother tongue), social characteristics (marital status, literacy, educational attainment, women’s status), and economic characteristics (employment status, occupation, income) also need to be considered when describing population characteristics:</p>
<p>Prepared by O.E. Akoth</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol>
<li>Census</li>
<li>National Survey</li>
<li>Registration of vital events</li>
<li>Demographic Studies</li>
</ol>
<p>The wider scope of demography is concerned only with population variables but also with relationships between population changes and other variables e.g.</p>
<ol>
<li>Social,</li>
<li>Economic,</li>
<li>Political,</li>
<li>Biological,</li>
<li>Genetic,</li>
<li>Geographical,</li>
<li>Intelligence and</li>
<li>Health.</li>
</ol>
<p>Population studies extend to applications of its data findings in a number of fields including the study of problems associated with demographic processes. The field of demographic studies is as broad as the interest in determining the consequences of population trends.</p>
<p>In a broader sense, additional characteristics such as ethnicity (race, mother tongue), social characteristics (marital status, literacy, educational attainment, women's status), and economic characteristics (employment status, occupation, income) also need to be considered when describing population characteristics:</p>
<ol>
<li>Census</li>
<li>National Survey</li>
<li>Registration of vital events</li>
<li>Demographic Studies</li>
</ol>
<p>Population studies are concerned not only with population variables but also with relationships between population changes &amp; other variables – social, economic, political, biological, genetic, geographical, environmental, health &amp; the like</p>
<p>Definition of Key Words</p>
<p>Prepared by O.E. Akoth</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol>
<li>Size refers to the number of persons in the population</li>
<li>Distribution refers to the arrangement of the population in space at a given time</li>
<li>Structure is the distribution of population among its sex &amp; age groupings</li>
<li>Change is the growth or decline of the total population or one of its structural units. The components of change total population are births, deaths, &amp; migrations</li>
<li>Age-Sex Composition of a population refers to the proportion of males &amp; females in different age-groups. It has a direct bearing on social, economic, health needs of communities or countries. In an "old" population, for example, the society has to arrange for the care of the elderly, &amp; the country's health system must be organized accordingly. In a "young" population, on the other hand, the country has to provide more schools, immunizations, &amp; economic support for the young</li>
<li>Net-Migration refers to the total number of persons added or subtracted from a population as a result of the combined effect of immigration &amp; emigration</li>
<li>Urbanization refers to mass migration of rural population into urban centers resulting in increasing the urban population &amp; growth of cities</li>
<li>Population Growth Rate (%/ year) is the rate at which a given population is expected to increase in a given period of time.</li>
<li>Population Doubling Time refers to the time that would take for a population to double. Because the population increase is on the compound interest formula, a 1% per year increase would cause the population to double in about 70 years. If the population is increasing at 3% per year, than the doubling time will be 23.3 years</li>
<li>Population Pyramid is a pictorial presentation of the age-sex composition of a population</li>
<li>Replacement Level Fertility (or Zero population growth) is activated when a couple has two births during their reproductive life, just enough to replace themselves. At a community scale, the replacement level is considered when there are, on the average, 2.1 births per woman, to compensate for child deaths</li>
<li>Momentum of Population Growth is the characteristic of population growth when a sharp decline in births does not bring in an immediate reduction in natural increase</li>
</ol>
<p>There are four ways in which the number of people in an area can change during two time periods t0 &amp; t1</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi></mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">o</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi><mo>−</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">D</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">I</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">O</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{Pt}1 = \mathrm{Pto} + (\mathrm{B} - \mathrm{D}) + (\mathrm{IM} - \mathrm{OM})</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">Pt</span></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7667em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">Pto</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathrm">B</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathrm">D</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">IM</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">OM</span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>Prepared by O.E. Akoth</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>B = number of live births to mothers in the area</p>
<p>D = number of residents died</p>
<p>IM = number of persons moving into the area fro permanent residence</p>
<p>OM = number of persons moving out of the area to live elsewhere</p>
<p>Thus the population of an area may change due to natural reasons (B – D) known as natural increase or due to migration (IM – OM) known as net-migration. Subsequently:</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mtext>Population&nbsp;Growth</mtext><mo>=</mo><mtext>Natural&nbsp;Increase</mtext><mo>+</mo><mtext>Net&nbsp;Migration</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\text{Population Growth} = \text{Natural Increase} + \text{Net Migration}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">Population&nbsp;Growth</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7778em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">Natural&nbsp;Increase</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8778em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">Net&nbsp;Migration</span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>While characteristic is an attribute of an individual (e.g. male, young, healthy, employed etc), composition is a property of a group of people. It describes how the total given population is constituted (e.g. 51% males, 20% below age 5, 85% healthy 7&amp; 30% employed etc).</p>
<p>Dependency Ratio is an index summarizing an age distribution. Strictly, this is the ratio of population who are economically not active to those who are economically active. However, due to the difficulties in defining economic activity in many countries, especially when international comparisons are made, a ratio of age group is used instead:</p>
<p>Population Composition</p>
<p>Dependency Ratio</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mtext>Children</mtext><mo>+</mo><mtext>Elderly</mtext><mo>×</mo><mn>100</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">= \text{Children} + \text{Elderly} \times 100</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7778em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">Children</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">Elderly</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">100</span></span></span></span></span></div>

<p>Pop 15 – 64 years</p>
<p>Dependency Ratio of Pakistan = 95.1</p>
<p>Dependency Ratio of UK = 66.5</p>
<p>&gt; Sex Ratio: The overall sex ratio is simply the ratio of males to females in the population &amp; is calculated by taking the number of males in a population &amp; dividing it by the number of females in the same population</p>
<p>Sex Ratio = <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mtext>Number&nbsp;of&nbsp;Males</mtext><mtext>Number&nbsp;of&nbsp;Females</mtext></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{\text{Number of Males}}{\text{Number of Females}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.2251em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8801em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">Number&nbsp;of&nbsp;Females</span></span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">Number&nbsp;of&nbsp;Males</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> × 100</p>

<p>Demographic Cycle: World history suggests that every nation passes through a demographic cycle.</p>
<p>The stages are:</p>
<ol>
<li>High Stationary Stage: characterized by high birth rate and high death rate</li>
<li>Early Expanding: The death rate begins to decline while birth rate remains unchanged</li>
<li>Late Expanding: The death rate declined still further and birth rate tend to fall</li>
<li>Low Stationary Stage: Low birth and low death rates</li>
<li>Declining Stage: birth rate is lower than the death rate and population starts declining</li>
</ol>
<p>&gt; Old Balance: (High fertility &amp; High Mortality). A large supply of births was necessary to compensate for the large number of deaths. MMR &amp; IMR extremely high
&gt; New Balance: (Low fertility &amp; Low Mortality) Represents an improved condition of human efficiency &amp; health, with fewer deaths considerably less efforts required to bring a generation to maturity. Production of agricultural &amp; industrial commodities is greater &amp; life style is more comfortable
&gt; Imbalance: (High Fertility &amp; Low Mortality) In between old &amp; new balance is the period of rapid natural increase. This growth is helpful for under-populated nations. Too fast growth of population leading economic, social &amp; political chaos (being faced by numerous developing countries including Pakistan)</p>
<ol>
<li>World Population Trend/ Population Dynamics: The rampant population growth is viewed as the greatest obstacle to the economic &amp; social development of the majority of peoples in the underdeveloped world</li>
</ol>
<p>Approximately 95% of population growth is in developing countries</p>
<p>Currently, 1/3 of the world population is &lt; 15, &amp; will soon enter the reproductive bracket, giving more potential for population growth</p>
<p>The expected number of births per woman, at current fertility rate is:</p>

<p>Economic implications: Due to population explosion there are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Short term pressure affects during 2-3 decade</li>
<li>Long term over next century and beyond economic affects</li>
</ol>
<p>Demographic Implications: In population with low birth and death rate, 20-30% of population is under 15; 9-13% is 65 or more. The median age for this population is 32 and there is increased demand for senior citizen</p>
<p>Environmental / Ecological Implications</p>
<p>Due to population explosion there are</p>
<p>Short term pressure affects during 2-3 decade</p>
<p>Long term over next century and beyond economic affects</p>
<p>Social / Political Implications</p>
<p>In population with low birth and death rate, 20-30% of population is under 15; 9-13% is 65 or more. The median age for this population is 32 and there is increased demand for senior citizens</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses-of-demographic-information">USES OF DEMOGRAPHIC INFORMATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses-of-demographic-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Demographic information can be used in:</p>
<ol>
<li>Economic Planning: by providing basic data needed planning:</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Population size,
b) Growth rate,
c) Available labor force.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Policy making: the data on growth rate for example can be used by the government to encourage family planning.</li>
</ol>
<p>147
Prepared by O.E. Akoth</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Administrative purposes: whether or not to sub-divide an administrative area mainly depends on the population to be served.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Political purposes: the number of constituencies in a given district depends on the population of the district.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Distribution of Social welfare: in institutions, facilities and services e.g. health, education, security, water supplies, transport, e.t.c. depend on the population of the area:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>i. The number of health institutions to be established in a given area depends on the population to be served.</p>
<p>ii. The number of primary schools to be established in an area depends on the population of the primary school going age.</p>
<p>iii. The capacity of water supply installation to supply an urban center depends on the population of the center’s catchment area besides other factors.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Health indicators: the health status of a community is easily portrayed by the various rates calculated in demography e.g.</li>
</ol>
<p>i. Mortality rates,</p>
<p>ii. Fertility rates,</p>
<p>iii. Morbidity rates,</p>
<p>iv. Birth rates and</p>
<p>v. Life expectancy.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>
<p>Social Research: Any social research must make use of some demographic information.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Distribution of communal Burden: a country like Kenya which has relied on fund raising [Harambee] for development of most of the social infrastructures like schools and</p>
</li>
</ol>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>health institutions has to allocate quotas to divisions, locations, sub-locations or villages primarily according to their populations.</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>Distribution of human resources: to determine human resources in terms of labor as a factor or economic production, its potential and actual exploitation [labor force, employed, underemployed and unemployed].</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="measurement-of-human-population">MEASUREMENT OF HUMAN POPULATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measurement-of-human-population" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health services apply demographic studies in several ways e.g.</p>
<p><strong>Fertility Measures</strong>: of a group of women reveals their performance in child bearing which in turn implies how their health may directly or indirectly be affected by the revealed fertility rate.</p>
<p><strong>Mortality Measure</strong>: of a population would reveal at what rate the people are dying. High mortality rate would indicate poor health which in turn would call for investigation to the causes in order to institute corrective measures.</p>
<p><strong>Average Life expectancy</strong>: of individual in a society indicates the general health status of the society.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-demographic-data">SOURCES OF DEMOGRAPHIC DATA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-demographic-data" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The raw materials of informal demography are data collected in:</p>
<ol>
<li>Population census,</li>
<li>Demographic sample survey,</li>
<li>Registration of vital events e.g.
i. Births,
ii. Deaths,
iii. Migrations and
iv. Marriages.</li>
<li>Compulsory national social security scheme records,</li>
<li>Records of establishments,</li>
</ol>
